Economic Special Issue

Statement of Purpose of Publication 163

This year marks the 60th anniversary of this newspaper. Based on the spirit of "old but vigorous" and "unceasing self-improvement," we have been devising plans to advance our work and meet the expectations of our readers. Unfortunately, the "September 18th Incident" and the Shanghai war followed one after another, hindering the progress of our work. Now that the national crisis has not yet been resolved, our colleagues at this newspaper are even more aware that to overcome the national crisis, we must be determined to "fulfill our respective responsibilities" and "take practical action." Therefore, based on this purpose, we will compile and produce a special economic supplement on commercial news every Monday, detailing the economic changes in China and abroad for the week, and compiling various important statistics for reference by those who are interested in the economy. Furthermore, in recent centuries, all political, social, and military issues among nations and internationally have used economic power as the object of their resolution and as their ultimate weapon. This is something that everyone should know and understand. Therefore, the general public should have some economic common sense to cope with these situations. Based on this goal, we will write articles separately to ensure that readers have a reasonable understanding of public and private economics. The scope of our future articles is tentatively set as follows:

(1) Economic Commentary: Provide commentary or forecasts on major domestic and international economic events each week to clarify the past and future situations.

(2) Investment Guidance and Statistics: In recent years, due to political instability, domestic capital has gradually concentrated in Shanghai. This has led to the increasing prosperity of Shanghai and the increasing economic hardship of the interior, which is not a good sign for China's future. With surplus capital flooding into Shanghai, speculation has become rampant, as evidenced by the recent public bond bidding and real estate business. This publication should focus on guiding legitimate investment avenues, introducing various stable Chinese and foreign stocks, bonds, and profitable new businesses. All related statistics and charts should be carefully organized and published as much as possible to fulfill our guiding responsibility, so that the surplus capital in society has a proper path to follow and the trend of speculation may be somewhat curbed.

(3) Investigation and Research of Industry and Commerce: China's current economic backwardness requires the urgent development of industry and commerce. This publication should first investigate the current situation and trends of industry and commerce, and then proceed to study the development and improvement plans. In particular, we should find ways to encourage and support domestic industrial products.

(4) Investigation and Research of Special Economic Organizations in China: China has long suffered from the aggression of foreign economic forces, gradually forming various special economic organizations such as compradors in foreign firms. The evolution and current status of such systems are all worthy of study to clarify the nature of these deformed organizations. In addition, the status of various existing economic organizations in China, such as folk mutual aid societies and various commercial practices, are also included in the investigation and research.

(5) Discussion and Translation of Economic Issues: In recent years, social thought in China has become complex and economic systems cannot be established. Academic discussions on various ideologies such as capitalism and fascism should be conducted to gain some understanding. In addition, valuable economic works from various countries should be translated and introduced to popularize knowledge.

In addition to the above outlines, surveys of important commodities such as rice, cotton, silk, coal, tea, oil, and wheat, research on financial and monetary issues, forecasts of trade and exchange rate changes, and introductions to famous economic works can be added at any time.

Furthermore, all the writings in this publication strive to be statistical, so that readers have numerical evidence and can be practical. We also plan to compile important economic statistics from January 1933 to provide a clear overview of the overall economic situation. This publication is in its initial stage, and there are many shortcomings. We hope that talents from all over the world will come forward and teach us. We would be most grateful.

The Issue of Cash Transportation to the Northeast 164

In the past three months, it has been rumored that 18 to 19 million yuan in cash has been transported from Shanghai to the Northeast. The general public does not know the real reason and believes that it is no different from collecting cash for them to purchase soybeans, a special product of the Northeast, for export to the United States to support Japan's foreign exchange rate. There have been many rumors and debates. Now, after detailed investigation, it is known that there are other special reasons. It is to supply the needs of the residents of the Northeast, which in turn has led to the relationship of deposit and remittance offsetting. Although it is an export from Shanghai, the cash transported is still scattered in the hands of farmers in the Northeast. In a transfer, it is still taken back to China proper by farmers traveling from the Northeast. Those who have lived in the Northeast generally know this. Therefore, the current cash transportation issue is not yet a problem, but how can the economic power of the compatriots in the Northeast break away from the control of foreigners? The people of the country should pay close attention to this. Now, according to the investigation, the following is recorded for reference by those who care about the Northeast's finance: 1. The Chinese population in the three northeastern provinces is said to be 30 million, of which about 70% are farmers. These 21 million farmers are not all natives; a small number are from Zhili, Shandong, and Henan provinces. They go to the Northeast every spring and return in winter. Each winter, they convert their harvest into cash and remit or carry it back to their hometown (because Northeast paper money cannot be used in China proper). Assuming that each person carries back 10 to 20 yuan, or even dozens of yuan, the transaction of remittance or the need for cash will suddenly increase by tens of millions of yuan every winter.

2. Most of these farmers from other provinces live in areas without banks in China proper. Due to the popularity of post offices, most of them have traditionally entrusted the post office to remit money back to China proper before returning home at the end of the year. The total amount of these post office and bank remittances amounts to no less than tens of millions of yuan each year. Recently, due to the withdrawal of the national postal service, it is not possible to remit all through banks. They do not trust the paper money of the Central Bank of Manchuria. Moreover, because Northeast paper money cannot circulate in China proper and cannot be brought back for use, they have to exchange all of it for cash and carry it with them. Moreover, the people of the Northeast are unsettled. Even the settled immigrants often exchange the paper money they have prepared for cash to seek security. This is why there is a huge demand for cash in the Northeast recently.

3. After the "September 18th Incident," the Chinese-run silver firms and banks in the Northeast continued to operate as before to maintain their original economic position. Those in Dalian, Yingkou, and other places in the south are also the same as before and have not changed. Moreover, due to the floods in northern Manchuria and the unrest in various places, people are uneasy and businesses are sluggish. The general public, with patriotic hearts, still deposits their savings in domestic silver firms and banks. Therefore, since the "September 18th Incident," the deposits of Chinese-owned silver firms and banks in the Northeast have seen unprecedented increases. However, because of the current situation in the Northeast, these firms cannot use their deposits in the Northeast and dare not store various types of paper money from the Northeast. Therefore, they transfer the deposits they have absorbed to Shanghai, Tianjin, and other places to ensure the safety of the depositors and to meet the needs of remittances or cash for the farmers from Zhili, Shandong, and Henan provinces returning home in winter. These silver firms cannot but take on the responsibility of regulating. A look at the sharp rise and special rise in the exchange rate between the Northeast and Shanghai and Tianjin can reveal a rough idea. With such a large amount of cash needed, they have to transport cash to supply it. However, this cash is ultimately brought back to their original home by the farmers from other provinces, so in reality, it will not remain in the Northeast.

4. The market in the Northeast has always traded in various non-convertible paper currencies and does not require cash. Recently, the pseudo-state unified the currency system, and the Japanese implemented an economic monopoly by exchanging various non-convertible paper currencies for paper money from the Central Bank of Manchuria, almost making the paper money of the Central Bank of Manchuria the legal currency for transactions. The Japanese only need to exchange gold tickets for paper money from the Central Bank of Manchuria or specie (Yokohama Specie Bank notes) or various types of paper money that have not yet been withdrawn to buy soybeans, and there is no need to rely on cash. However, Chinese-owned silver firms and banks, struggling in a harsh environment, cannot but prepare for withdrawals and encashment.

From this, it can be seen that the Japanese are implementing a policy of economic monopoly in the Northeast more and more every day. The paper money wages that our farmers have earned through hard work throughout the year cannot be brought back to their original homes for use, so they have no choice but to entrust the silver firms to remit them back. If their hometown is a place that cannot be remitted by silver firms and there is no post office to remit, then they can only exchange it for cash and bring it back. If the Chinese silver firms in the Northeast do not transport cash to provide for their needs, wouldn't they be sitting idly by while these millions of people are stranded in the Northeast and become starving people? However, the Japanese certainly hope that these millions of compatriots have money but cannot remit it back and instead hoard the paper money of the Central Bank of Manchuria to celebrate the success of their plan.

The Soviet Banking System Translated by Wu Hongshou 165

The Soviet State Bank has recently completed ten years of successful operation. The Soviet State Bank is the only issuing bank and central credit institution in the country, so it is a major factor in improving the national economy. In addition, the State Bank has special and important tasks for the production of a stable currency system, the development of industry and commerce, and the implementation of the economic policies of social construction.

The establishment of the State Bank in 1921 and the special franchise for the issuance of gold-backed banknotes (Chervontzi) in 1922 were preliminary steps in implementing the construction of a stable currency system and concentrating capital. The initial capital accumulation did not include depreciated banknotes. On May 1, 1932, the State Bank's integrated reserve included gold, platinum, and fixed foreign currency valued at 722.8 (million units) rubles (equivalent to more than 37 million US dollars). On the same date, the bank's capital and surplus totaled 576,300,000 rubles (equivalent to more than 29.6 million US dollars), a six-fold increase compared to October 1, 1924. The State Bank's assets have increased rapidly, from 155 million rubles on October 1, 1922, to 18 trillion rubles (equivalent to 9.4 trillion US dollars) on May 1, 1932. The average monthly circulation this year has reached 5.5 trillion rubles, far exceeding the 100 million rubles from 1922 to 1923. Branches are spread throughout the country, and now more than 2,700 institutions have been established.

▲The Soviet Bank's Task for Economic Policy▲

The Soviet Union has no private banks. All private banks were nationalized in December 1917. Therefore, this bank became an indispensable part of the policy, jointly proceeding to achieve its common goal, which is to support and implement economic policies. This bank has an important task for concentrating and redistributing national benefits. The main parties of the Soviet Bank are the various organizations and businesses in the national economy.

The only feature of the Soviet banking system is the division of short-term lending and long-term lending operations. This approach has been gradually implemented. Since its inception, short-term lending has been largely concentrated in the State Bank. After the reform of 1930, the State Bank became the only source of short-term lending. The State Bank also operates some long-term lending, especially in agriculture. By May 1932, all long-term lending was allocated to four designated banks.

▲The Development of the State Bank▲

The development of the State Bank over the past decade is a reflection of the development of the national economy. When the State Bank was first established, it was after the adoption of the New Economic Policy. The level of the domestic economy was extremely low due to the results of the world and domestic wars. Industrial production only reached 20% of the pre-war level, agricultural production was less than 50%, and the transportation industry was almost completely bankrupt. This newly established State Bank took on the important task of restoring industry, agriculture, and the organization of domestic commerce. During this period, the main tasks of the State Bank, in addition to establishing a stable currency and credit system, were to cultivate the development of socialized industry and commerce.

Due to the surge in its sources, the State Bank was able to expand its lending operations to meet the needs of the rapidly developing industrial and commercial business operations. The State Bank's lending to various national economies increased from 525 (million) rubles on October 1, 1924, to 2.9 trillion rubles (October 1, 1928), and then to 5.4 trillion rubles (May 1, 1932). This number is distributed among the following major businesses:

(Million Rubles) (Percentage)

Domestic Supply and State-Owned Enterprises 1519.4 28.1

Agriculture 708.2 13.1

Heavy Industry 674.1 12.5

Consumer Cooperative 659.0 12.2

Timber Industry 57.19 10.6

Light Industry 554.1 10.3

Production Cooperative 114.6 2.1

The State Bank also manages all of the Soviet Union's large foreign trade. All Soviet foreign trade receipts and expenditures are handled by the State Bank. Payments are made by branches around the world. The Soviet Union's centralized and planned management of foreign payments is very reliable. Since the period when the Soviet Union established trade relations with foreign countries, there has never been a single unreliable payment.

The Soviet State Bank is governed by two parts: the Council and the Board of Directors. The Soviet Minister of Finance is the Chairman of the Council. The Council meets at least twice a year to set out the business outline and appoint directors. The Chairman and Vice-Chairman of the Board of Directors are appointed by the Minister of Civil Affairs.

The steady and rapid development of industrial and commercial production and the gradual concentration of all major production and commerce in the hands of socialization have enabled the State Bank and the Soviet currency system to increase their financial stability. Due to various new developments, the credit system had to undergo a reform, because the credit system before 1930 was mainly based on bills of exchange.

▲Reform of the Credit System▲

The credit reform of January 1930 stipulated the abolition of all old-style commercial credit and replaced it with direct bank credit. Domestic and cooperative enterprises are therefore no longer allowed to supply goods or services to each other on credit. Therefore, the State Bank became the sole short-term lending institution. This lending is provided to buyers, not to sellers in the form of bill discounting.

Subsequently, due to the discovery of certain weaknesses and distortions in the credit reform regulations, supplementary decrees were promulgated in 1931 (January, March, June). The implementation of these decrees was able to eliminate the mechanical state of previous transactions, focus on the importance of contracts between buyers and sellers, determine the task of the State Bank, guarantee the main conditions of bank credit, and make the approval of lending based on economic or production plans and the implementation of timely repayment. These decrees have proven well in consolidating economic accounting, tightening business cycles, increasing the interest of economic organizations in rationalizing production, reducing costs, accumulating surpluses, and improving credit discipline in the past.

▲Long-Term Credit Bank▲

The State Bank occupies a prominent position in the Soviet banking system and is the only issuing and short-term credit institution. However, in addition, the long-term credit bank also undertakes a most important function, which is to regulate construction capital.

The allocation of construction capital has increased frequently in recent years. The total number for this year is 24.2 trillion rubles. Under this circumstance, the most important thing is to urge each design to be absolutely responsible for the implementation of the plan within its specified time frame and to reduce its costs. In order to make the system of regulating construction funds (giving loans based on the actual implementation of the design) more precise and to expand the economic accounting of construction projects, a decree was announced on May 5, 1932 to reorganize the organization of long-term credit. The decree centralized all long-term credit operations into four types of banks, each bank taking on the task of regulating the fixed construction capital in the national economy.

The first bank is the Industrial Bank (Proinbank), which focuses on regulating state-owned domestic and foreign enterprises belonging to the management of heavy industry, light industry, timber industry, supply industry, and foreign trade, and belonging to the Labor Arbitration Committee. The second is the Agricultural Bank (Selkhozbank), which specializes in regulating the investment capital of all state-owned farms, transportation industries, and joint farms. The third is the Cooperative Bank (Yeskcbank), which specializes in regulating the construction funds of all cooperative organizations (excluding family cooperatives). The fourth is the Municipal Bank (Tsekombank), which specializes in regulating municipal public utilities, the construction of dormitories, and the establishment of new cities. All three banks other than the Cooperative Bank circulate with non-refundable subsidies and long-term loans. The Cooperative Bank only has long-term loans.

A large amount of construction funds for industry and electricity are non-refundable loans. The majority of these loans are provided by the government treasury. However, all industrial organizations must pay a portion of their surplus into the bank. Therefore, when many factories and power plants are established, the surplus paid by each factory will also increase, and the loans in the treasury budget will decrease accordingly.

At the beginning of this year, the Industrial and Commercial Bank, which operates long-term lending, has established 32 branches and has representatives stationed in most branches of the State Bank. In order to have adequate contact with the actual construction plan, each branch is established in the area where most of the construction is carried out. As a result of direct management and the strict accounting of engineering supply agencies by bank agencies, there is considerable encouragement for the economy.

In addition to the State Bank and long-term lending banks regulating the national economy, there are also savings banks spread throughout the country. At the beginning of this year, the total amount of their deposits has exceeded 1 trillion rubles.

The steady operation of Soviet economic development and its perfect lending system (this system is the most important element in the entire economic plan) enable the Soviet banking system to be in a stable position and have been able to avoid inflexibility. Another reason for the stability of the Soviet banking system and currency system is the balance of the government's annual budget without any shortages.

The Soviet financial budget is based on meeting economic needs. Therefore, of the total expenditure of 20.4 trillion rubles in 1932, 15.3 trillion, or 75%, was used to regulate the national economy (industry, agriculture, transportation, commerce, post, and telegraph and other industries). Only 1.5 trillion rubles, or 7.5%, was used for national defense and management.

The main source of tax revenue for the Soviet financial budget is the socialized national economy. In addition to this, only a small portion is taxed by the people. There are two types of payments from the socialized part: a portion of the surplus of state-owned enterprises and the Business Turnover Tax. Changes in tax rates affect prices. Because prices must be restricted by the government, the Business Turnover Tax is not taken from the people. In 1931, the tax revenue from the socialized part was 15.9 trillion rubles, which is 77.6% of the total tax revenue. The tax revenue from the people was 2.9 trillion rubles, only 14%.

Although the government's financial system has a relatively stable foundation, the rapid progress of Soviet industry does not reduce the bank's heavy responsibilities in the future. In fact, with the increase in national economic resources, it is even more important for Soviet banks to allocate these resources and redistribute them to further the development of the country and the happiness of the people.

Translated from the American Banking Magazine, September 1932

Conversion Method of Chinese and Foreign Wheat Prices 166

Wang Zongpei

Modern commerce is becoming increasingly internationalized, and the prices of various major commodities mostly fluctuate with the international market. Shanghai is an important commercial market in China and one of the world's major trading ports. Therefore, domestic and foreign market prices are interrelated. However, due to the differences in weights and measures and the differences in monetary units, there is a conversion between prices according to different countries. This type of conversion is difficult for outsiders to understand. This article is a draft of the algorithm based on the investigation of non-professionals. I hope that experts in the industry will point out the errors. This publication welcomes such discussion and research manuscripts and hopes that they will continue to benefit readers. Sincerely, the editor notes that in the recent ten years or so, various parts of our country have suffered from natural disasters and man-made disasters, and the people have been unable to make a living. The rural economy has collapsed, farmers have left their hometowns, and the land has been abandoned. Production has been reduced. The output is quite abundant, and the export of wheat, which has been sold overseas in the past, has also decreased year by year. The import of foreign wheat has increased with the years. In recent years, the raw material supply of various flour mills has also relied on foreign wheat. This is because the quality of foreign wheat is better than that of domestic wheat, and better records can be obtained for flour production. Therefore, it is favored by various flour mills, causing a reversal of the guest-host relationship.

Foreign wheat occupies an important position in the Chinese market today. The varieties of imported wheat are mainly Australian wheat, Canadian wheat, and American wheat. Therefore, the harvest yields and price increases and decreases in these places are sufficient to affect the Shanghai wheat market, and the conversion method of Chinese and foreign wheat prices has become the focus of research for manufacturers and speculators.

The difference between Chinese and foreign wheat prices lies in the difference between the quotation unit and the standard currency. The standard wheat of the Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Cake Exchange must weigh between 139 jin and 140 jin to be qualified for trading. The trading unit is "vehicle," and each vehicle is about 880 jin. The market price is calculated by "dan" (100 jin). For example, the recent market price is about 3 liang and 4 qian per dan. The market price of foreign wheat, with North America as the center, is said to be based on Australian wheat as the selling standard in Canada, while American wheat is concentrated in Chicago. The market price is calculated by "bushel" and the standard currency is US dollars. For example, the recent market price is about 50 US cents per "bushel."

Because of the different calculation units and gold and silver standard currencies in the Chinese and foreign wheat markets, there is a common conversion simplification method in the flour and wheat industry. According to people in the industry, the foreign wheat market price is converted to the Shanghai market price. First, "33" is used to divide the price per bushel. The quotient is then divided by the US exchange rate to obtain the Shanghai yuan equivalent of each stone of foreign wheat. If you want to convert it into the price per dan, you only need to divide it by 139 or 140. The formula is as follows:

(Foreign wheat price ÷ 33) ÷ US exchange rate ÷ 140 = Shanghai yuan equivalent of the price per dan of Australian wheat... (1)

For example, on October 17, the Canadian telegram reported that October wheat was valued at 48 and 1/8 US cents per bushel. Assuming that the US exchange rate on that day was 30 and 5/16 US dollars per 100 Shanghai yuan, then the market price per dan of Canadian wheat would be equivalent to 3 liang, 4 qian, 3 fen, and 6 li of Shanghai silver. The formula is as follows:

(48.125 US dollars ÷ 33 shi) ÷ 30.3125/100 US dollars ÷ 1.40 dan = 3.436 liang of Shanghai yuan

The thing that should be paid attention to in the first formula is "Divide the foreign wheat market price by "33"". This "33" should be 1.33 shi or 3.3 dou, because the US volume is 3.4031251 dou or 0.34031251 shi per bushel. The industry custom abandons the more accurate "0.34" and uses "0.33" to divide the foreign wheat market price, which is actually incomprehensible. It is speculated that it is easier to remember and calculate when dividing by "33". Therefore, it seems that the result may be more accurate if "34" is used to divide. It is perplexing that the industry custom abandons the more precise "·34" and uses "·33" to divide the foreign wheat market price.

Dividing the foreign wheat market price by "·33" or "·34" obtains the US dollar equivalent of the foreign wheat price per dan.

(Australian foreign wheat market price ÷ .33) = (.48125 ÷ .33) = 1.458 US dollars

Then, divide the US dollar equivalent of the foreign wheat price per dan by the US exchange rate to obtain the Shanghai yuan equivalent of the foreign wheat price per dan as follows:

(1.458 US dollars ÷ 30.125/100) = 4.811 Shanghai yuan liang (the Shanghai yuan equivalent of the price per shi of foreign wheat)

If you want to compare it with Chinese wheat, you still need to divide it by "139" or "140" to convert it into the Shanghai yuan equivalent of the foreign wheat price per dan as follows:

(4.811 Shanghai yuan liang ÷ 1.40 dan) = 3.436 Shanghai yuan liang (the price per dan)

Furthermore, if "·34" is substituted for "·33" in the first formula, the result will be smaller than the former. The new formula is as follows:

(Foreign wheat price ÷ 34 shi) ÷ US exchange rate ÷ 1.40 dan = Shanghai yuan equivalent of the foreign wheat price per but... (2)

Now, let's include the example of October 17 for calculation:

(.48125 US dollars ÷ .34 shi) ÷ 30.3125/100 US dollars ÷ 1.40 dan = 3.335 Shanghai yuan liang

Compared with the two, the latter is calculated to be 1 qian and 1 li of Shanghai silver less than the former. It seems that the calculation is better than the former, and the theory that foreign wheat can be 1 or 2 qian more expensive than Chinese wheat seems to have a considerable relationship with the inaccuracy of the calculation.

Short Story

New Wedding Night (4) 167

— Bing Xin

(3)

Miss Xiu’s eyes were so swollen she couldn’t open them. She curled up her legs to her stomach, completely like a shrimp, tightly shrinking and not daring to move even slightly, afraid of waking up that ugly and loathsome old monkey – the honorable title she had given him – whom she had never encountered even in her dreams. Thinking of the events of last night, she couldn’t help but tremble again, and the area around her eyes became moist again. Two cold tears rolled down her cheeks, stopping on her tender chin.

“Oh, yesterday I used all the strength of my life to resist, so I was able to hold on until today. I am still myself, my own soul, my own body, my own ego – but what about tonight? I have no strength left, my right hand is seriously injured and can barely move. Oh, Heaven, what am I going to do?

Aunt is too unreasonable. She is still a woman who understands poetry, books, and etiquette, and her sons are all working outside. Why would she do such a heartless and inhumane thing? Marrying me off to such a hideous man, the ugliest man in the world, is more painful and torturous than cutting off my head or slicing off my flesh piece by piece. Humph, matchmaker, what a bloodless murderer. Her own daughters run off to marry freely, so why does she control me and plot against me?

Mother is too pitiful, she has cried countless times for me, I cannot blame her. Father is too cruel, may Buddha punish him, and when I become a ghost, I will take revenge. He is too heartless, how could he marry me to such a person….”

Floating in Miss Xiu’s mind, apart from resentment, grief, sadness, and disappointment, was the hideous face of that terrifying old monkey. Moreover, the impression of that face seemed to be glued on with lacquer, never to be removed. “Oh, you’re awake! Don’t cry anymore, it’s unseemly for others to hear. Tonight we can have a good time…”

Heavens, it turned out that the hideous, terrifying monkey face had already come to Miss Xiu’s side. She was so frightened that she almost screamed, but suddenly she heard whispering voices from next door, so she had to endure it and turn her face inward.

Taking advantage of the opportunity to go to the toilet, Miss Xiu, with her hair disheveled, ran to the house of her matchmaker – her aunt. Originally, she had just arrived yesterday at this large courtyard of over a hundred households in Youzhachong, and did not know where her aunt lived, only that it was not far from her. When she quietly walked out of the back door, she saw a cowherd. After she asked for directions, she ran frantically. The child thought she was a guest, because her appearance was so different from yesterday.

Baoying Garden suddenly became lively: neighbors from near and far, both men and women, old and young, all ran to see this beautiful and strange bride.

"Quickly go inside, close the door, it's so embarrassing to have so many people watching."

Aunt was so angry that her face turned ashen. She felt that Miss Xiu was too disrespectful to her, not only because she was her niece, but also because she was the matchmaker herself.

Scolding 168

When joy reaches its peak, one "unconsciously moves one's hands and feet" – the natural expression of true feelings is indeed so uncontrollable. At the same time, if the stimulation that the outside world gives people is too deep, then the strong reaction evoked by the stimulation will also make people uncontrollably stomp their feet and beat their chests, forcing them to scold.

But in the eyes of hypocrites, scolding is extremely barbaric. Although they go against their conscience and do many bad things to harm others and benefit themselves, on the surface they are full of sweet words, trying not to reveal a trace. If anyone wants to complain or vent the accumulated anger in their heart, no matter how frank and straightforward they are, they will always strongly oppose it, no, severely interfere. In this era, the authority of hypocrites is high above others, so people's true feelings are often covered up by fierce flames.

In fact, the R-B-S reaction formula has absolutely no exceptions. We coldly observe that since there are injustices everywhere, there are things that deserve to be scolded everywhere. The so-called scolding, as long as it is serious criticism and fearless resistance, then the extension of justice may begin from this. Like now, some are tyrannical, some are昏淫無道, some brothers are quarreling, some are shamelessly betraying their principles, some are falling and committing suicide, and so on, even to the point of selling their daughters for glory and recognizing enemies as fathers; there are so many strange shapes and forms that it is simply countless – frankly speaking, who does not deserve to be scolded severely? As a joke, if we want to meet the demand, we should quickly set up several crash courses in scolding, which would not be too much.

The more you fear scolding, the more ugly things there are for people to scold, and the more you can't help but scold. If you don't want people to scold, unless you are willing to wash your heart and renew your life, break out of the dark encirclement, and move forward towards the bright path.

To think more about the people who scold, it's not good to say "laugh and scold as I please," so just casually and slowly scold, being afraid of scolding when it comes to scolding, or even scolding first and then not scolding. Mi Heng beat the drum and scolded Cao, his voice and expression were fierce, and he would rather die than yield. This is the spirit worth emulating! Otherwise, even if you are brave enough to scold everywhere, scolding people to the point of no return, it is still thousands of miles away from the natural expression of true feelings.

The Crossroads of the Times and Love 5 169

— Zhang Ziping

"Now they have moved to live in Hong Kong. Your sister scolds the Guangzhou authorities every day. What she says is very funny. She says that my brother's embezzlement of public funds was instructed by the authorities. Otherwise, how would he dare to be so bold? Once someone reports him, they will push the responsibility onto my brother. I think it's fortunate. When will there be an end to corrupt officials?

"I've said too much, I'll write again later. Goodbye. Let me say, I am your Peizhu, respectfully. November 10."

(3)

Liu Peizhu's sister, Peizhen, is the second daughter-in-law of the well-known compradore-class Ren Qiming in Shanghai. Her husband, Ren Jinhua, is the most fashionable talent in modern China – a Master of Economics from Harvard University in the United States. He is currently a first-class counselor in the Ministry of Finance, only going to Beijing once a month to collect his salary. The rest of the time he spends leisurely in Shanghai. The most time he spends is at dance halls, followed by playing mahjong. When Haiquan set off from Guangzhou to Shanghai, his sister told him that Liu Peizhen lived at No. 45, H Lane, Avenue Joffre in the French Concession of Shanghai, and asked him to bring some southern food and tea to Shanghai as a courtesy when visiting the Ren family.

"Can't you buy anything in Shanghai? Asking him to bring these boring things is annoying, isn't it?" What do you know? The gift is light, but the sentiment is heavy." His sister smiled and scolded her husband. The brother-in-law then walked away with a smile. Haiquan immediately thought that China was finished. Because the Chinese nation – especially the male compatriots – are too unprogressive and too unambitious. On weekdays, those big and small revolutionary heroes who grind their fists and palms and talk about revolution until their faces are red and their foreheads are bulging, kneel down and soften in front of women, abandoning their former positions and losing their former ambitions. Look at the great men of China today, which one is not controlled by their wives? – not afraid of their wives, then afraid of their concubines, not afraid of their concubines, then afraid of their mistresses. After Haiquan arrived in Shanghai, he was very unwilling to visit those people who obviously had class distinctions in material enjoyment. He knew that a certain foreign firm was the Ren family's liaison office, so he attached his name card to the food that his sister asked him to bring and gave it to the foreign firm to forward. He only made excuses that he would visit them after clarifying the matters of the school.

Probably his brother-in-law and Peizhu had both sent letters to Peizhen. Haiquan indirectly heard from Mr. Zeng that the Ren family on Avenue Joffre hoped that he would come to their house to play. So he felt that he was too neurotic and too arrogant, and was a bit unfair to the Ren family. At the same time, he also received a letter from his sister, scolding him for not visiting those relatives for a long time, which was too impolite.

Helpless, one Sunday morning, he decided to take a trip to the Ren family. He had heard people say that when visiting friends in Shanghai, it is best to do so around ten or eleven in the morning, because they are usually not at home in the afternoon and evening.

Woman… 170

— Qi Wen

Under the character for "woman," although there is usually a character for "person" or "child," just like under the character for "man," the men rarely consider the women to be the same as themselves, as "people" or "children." When Russia still had an emperor, they had a saying that "a hen is not a bird, and a woman is not a person." Our own "Great Accomplished Sage" also sighed, "Only women and petty men are difficult to raise!" Today, the women of Russia, which no longer has an emperor, according to people who have observed the new Russia, have not only become "people," but also have a tendency to surpass men; but in China, women are still difficult to raise; on the contrary, they are considered easy to raise, and are played with, and even played with to the extreme, nothing can be added.

Those who consider women difficult to raise are always friends who are not very financially well-off. They see others marrying a wife, although they have spent a lot of betrothal money, and they are still unwilling to get into the sedan chair happily, which is already frightening. Even when they see an advertisement for a pair of women's silk stockings in the glass window of a department store, selling for only eighteen yuan at a cheap price, they are sure to be stunned.

But on the other hand, it seems that anyone can afford to raise a woman. If we flip through a daily newspaper, the advertisements for women's products are of course drawn with beautiful women "with charming smiles"; even the advertisements for medicines specially for depraved men to inject or take are mostly modern girls "with beautiful eyes"; the hand in the cigarette advertisement holding that "golden tobacco silk" and "reasonable price" cigarette will always be a jade-like slender hand; the picture in the advertisement for medicine for corns is also of a beauty with her jade toes raised. Even a long, rectangular eyebrow painting in the supplement of the newspaper, nine times out of ten, has to rely on a fashionable woman, as if inviting contributors, saying: This magazine specially hires women to entertain. As for illustrated magazines, without female high school graduates, the editors would naturally be disappointed, and the readers would probably not be able to enjoy it with relish... In short, although a woman is nominally a "person," she is actually a "thing"!

So what should be done? It's easy, that is, women only need to regard themselves as "people," and men should not regard them as "things." As for the benefits after both men and women regard each other as "people"? At least the tragic and ugly dramas between the sexes that are specially supplied to social news can be reduced.

The World's Tallest Building – The Skyscraper 171

— Qiong

"What is the tallest building in the world?" If anyone asks this.

"Of course, it's New York's Woolworth Building!" I think you must answer this way. However, in fact, this is not the case. The glory of the Woolworth Building has long become a dream of the past, and the current tallest building is the Empire State Building, known as the Skyscraper.

This building was completed in May last year, is eighty-five stories high, and has 20,000 residents, almost equal to the population of a small city.

So where is this Skyscraper? Of course, it's in New York. Originally, tall buildings were a specialty of New York. According to recent statistics, there are 377 buildings with more than 20 floors in the United States, and New York accounts for half of them. So this tall building is in New York again, which is not surprising at all.

Now let me briefly introduce this Empire State Building. The roof of this Skyscraper has an airship mooring station, which is an unprecedented innovation in the world. Because it is too high, there must be high-speed elevators. Otherwise, even if you transport a small item from the bottom to the top floor, you will have to walk until dark. So there must be an elevator that can go up to sixty floors in one minute.

A few years ago, the aforementioned Woolworth Building was indeed the darling of the world, with fifty-eight floors, about seven and a half times the size of Tokyo's "Marunouchi" in Japan. But three years ago, the Manhattan Bank Building with sixty-five floors and the Chrysler Building with sixty-eight floors suddenly appeared, so the Woolworth Building was no longer a darling. When this Skyscraper was born last year, it fell directly to fourth place.

As for the reason for the appearance of this Skyscraper, it is of course inevitable that real estate entrepreneurs are competing, because tall buildings are easy to promote and easy to rent out. Moreover, Americans have a desire to create "the world's first." For example, if someone in a certain place has a tall building, "Okay, I will definitely not admit defeat, even if I borrow money, I will build one." So this tall building was produced in this competitive spirit. However, this is ultimately one aspect of observation. The fundamental reason is that the United States is a land of gold. "As long as you have money, you can do anything." This saying is the real reason for the appearance of the Skyscraper.

Swiss Girl 172

— Wan Ju

The French philosopher Pascal once said: From the point of view of behavior, good and evil are different problems depending on the place. In other words, human behavior is regional. What is called evil here is called beauty there. In this place, a certain behavior is ridiculous to the general public, but in that place, it is praised by the general public. Indeed, the so-called "custom" is a very incredible and very interesting thing. Stendhal has a work called "On Love," in which he describes the customs of the girls in the Berne area of Switzerland, which is quite interesting.

The behavior of Swiss women in their youth is romantic and innocent; and the families there also have a special attitude towards this behavior. It is said that a famous French officer once had to spend the night in a very remote and beautiful valley in Oberland due to mountain climbing. After arriving in the mountains, he stayed at the home of an official in the valley, who was the richest and most powerful person in the area. When this guest entered, he noticed a very charming girl of sixteen. This girl was the daughter of the host. That night, there happened to be a village dance party; because this girl was so beautiful and moving, the officer could not help but try to get close to her and flatter her. Finally, he mustered up the courage to ask her if he could sneak into her room at night. The girl replied: "No, I sleep with my cousin; but I can come to your room at night." After dinner, the traveler stood up. The beautiful girl took a lamp and led him to his room; seeing this situation, he thought that he could enjoy some pleasure tonight.

But this girl said with an innocent and romantic look: "No, I should ask my mother's permission first." This sentence was like a bolt from the blue, scaring the soul out of him, but before he could stop her, she had already gone out; the officer had no choice but to embolden himself and follow her, lurking outside the living room built of wooden boards to eavesdrop on what they were saying. He heard the girl coquettishly asking her mother to allow her what she hoped for; as a result, she achieved her goal. The old woman said to her husband, who was already lying on the bed: "Old man, don't you agree to allow Torini to spend the night with that officer?" "I am very willing," her old husband replied; "like this kind of person, I would be willing to lend him my woman to spend the night." Then the old woman said to Torini: "Well, go! But be brave, don't take off your skirt..."

At dawn, the girl got up from the guest's bed, she was still pure and flawless. The traveler respected her wishes that night and did not force her to do what she considered excessive. She tidied up the bedding and made coffee and milk to bring to the officer. Then she sat on the bed and had breakfast with him. After breakfast, she cut a piece of her corset covering her breasts and gave it to him, saying: "Keep this as a souvenir of this happy night! I will never forget this night..." So, she gave the officer one last kiss and fled like a startled swan, and he never saw her again.

"Old Youth" 173

— Zifang

It is said that in ancient China there was Lao Tzu, who had white hair and beard before he was born from his mother's womb, which may be completely credible; otherwise, why are there so many young people now who are so old and irresistible before they even leave school?

Their entire lives: eating, sleeping, wearing clothes; their lifelong plans: becoming officials, getting rich, marrying wives.

Our society is such an old society, and our youth is such an old youth; what is said about "catching up with the evolution of the world" is really dreaming with your eyes open – just wait and see people's "table dancing"!

Talking Points

Training Women's Army 174

— Fo

Since the September 18th Incident, Japan has been using a challenging attitude towards the world's powers everywhere, and the emotions are very bad, which will inevitably lead to a second world war. Therefore, it is actively preparing for war. After all, Japan is small and sparsely populated, and cannot withstand a single gamble. Therefore, the Tokyo Higher Girls' School Principals' Conference resolved to arm 35,000 female students in Tokyo and subject them to rigorous military training. It is heard that the Ministry of the Army is very supportive and has agreed to allocate 35,000 rifles, as well as pistols, poison gas defense equipment, etc., and start training from next spring. From then on, a large number of women soldiers will appear on the world stage.

Any militaristic country, although it has a system of universal conscription, the conscription only extends to men, and there is no news of women. Even the heroes who participate in the war mostly volunteer to fight bravely, and are not passively forced into the army. Now that Japan is forcing women to receive military training, and extending it further, men who are only ten years old can also be forced to go to the front line as sacrificial livestock. The situation after that is that the humans produced by the Creator are nothing more than targets for artillery fire and bombs. Please be aware, please understand, the so-called Nine-Power Treaty, Washington Conference, Disarmament Conference, etc., don't go to build empty shelves and put on a华容道anymore, tear down the peepshow, everyone desperately creates some citizens to be the sacrifices of the warlords.

Or say, no, "Japan's training of women soldiers has another special and wonderful use. Japan has always been famous for its good use of the beauty trap. Don't you see that when the investigation team went to Japan this time, no matter what meetings or banquets were held, they selected beautiful women to participate in the welcome. Assuming that once a war breaks out, driving five or six thousand娇艶and charming women to the front to fight, I ask, would the enemy still have the heart to use airplanes and artillery to carry out the means of煑鶴焚琴? It's really an excellent beauty trap.

Literature and Art

Feelings on Passing Baolong Mountain 175

— Sun Choucheng

Yesterday I met Jishi, who showed me his recent work, "Feelings on Passing Baolong Mountain," in the form of five-character ancient poems. Touched by the scenery, he couldn't help but look back. I will transcribe it as follows to fill this magazine.

In the past, when I traveled to Long Mountain, I saw the mountain colors and was very happy. I competed to be the first with my cane, forgetting the distance when climbing. The dangerous pavilion was like the round mountain, and the wild flowers reminded me of fragrant orchids. Now I pass this mountain again, and the mood is as light as water. How could the mountain have changed its appearance? It is all due to the endless chaos. Women and children leave their fields, and half of their neighbors die. Yesterday, when I passed Lotus City, my eyes were full of scars. The sick bones lay in the stone fields, and the鳩形called out. Feeling this, my tears wet my lap, crisscrossing and unstoppable. I cannot enjoy the wine, and I do not see the beauty of the flowers. Because I know that bitterness and joy are all in people's minds.

Sunday 176

— Gu Lou

Is this also considered a new trick?

The arrival of Sunday, for me, who is extremely poor, (with a fake satin robe from 1929 inside and a cloth shirt from 1932 outside, the length is compared, more stylish than the long robes and shorts of modern girls,) is of course commonplace, and I will never be like those modern young people, busy planning how to spend the day.

Last Sunday was an exception. It was probably around 4 o'clock in the afternoon when my old friend Mr. L, whom I hadn't seen for months, suddenly came to me. After a long separation, he invited me to go to the movies with him. At first, I declined on the grounds that I was busy with my studies, but in the end, I couldn't resist his kindness, so I pulled up my sleeves and went out with him.

When we arrived at the entrance of the N Theater, it was exactly 5:32. We were one step late, so we had to taste the door being closed. Just as we were unwilling to advance or retreat, someone suddenly said that he had a ticket for sale. I looked at the ticket and couldn't help but laugh, because the ticket was only half of one, and there was no "Pass" mark left on it. Unexpectedly, he thought our clothes were antiques and tried to cheat us. Finally, he also said that if the ticket was invalid, he could have his head cut off. At the same time, he blew his right hand toward his neck. I couldn't help but say to him humorously: "Keep your head! Throw your head to the Northeast, then it would not be a waste for your head to be on your neck." Royalties are donated to the Northeast Volunteer Army

— I

Dearest Juhua,

Do you know how empty I feel at this moment! When you are not by my side again.

Empty sky, empty room, empty mood, ah! Everything is empty, so empty that it frightens me, dear Ju sister! Where are you now? Why haven't you come yet? Can you bear to let me die of emptiness?

My beloved, I am waiting for you, waiting for you to warm my heart, waiting for you to kiss away my tears.

Your poor Zilang, 9:10 AM on the 11th.

My darling:

How happy I am, so happy that words cannot describe it. Isn't it? What I have been pursuing all my life is you. Now you are mine, and will always be mine. I have gotten my darling, so why shouldn't I be happy? Is there anything happier than this in the world?

Darling! My darling! My fiancée!

I will always savor the happiest scene of last night, when you stretched out your hand and nestled in my arms, letting me put the ring on your finger.

Your fiancé, morning of the 12th.

My dear:

I bet you are lying in bed with a flushed face, gazing at my photo, imagining our future happiness, aren't you?

That's right, we should work harder to get closer to happiness, while we are young. Please don't forget our appointment at 3 pm tomorrow. Now let me send you a passionate postal kiss.

Yours, evening of the 13th.

My sweetheart:

As soon as I think of the scene yesterday afternoon, my heart keeps pounding. Ah! Your body temperature, your red lips, your…

Happiness, happiness, the highest happiness in life!

I hope to have such an opportunity again. No, a hundred times, a thousand times, even ten thousand times.

The one in your heart, the night of the 14th, before going to bed. By the way, your request is very right, we should get married right away. But I think after we get married, we may not have such happiness as we have now, right? Dear, I wish we could maintain our current relationship for quite a long time.

Forever loving you, Zilang, the 16th.

Ju sister:

Hey! Why are you always unwilling to believe me? Do I have the slightest bit of falsehood towards you? Only heaven knows!

Aren't you coming today? Zilang, the 18th.

Ju sister:

You are so selfish, you always treat me as the worst person in the world. I really don't understand what you mean.

You should come once, I am waiting for you in ×× Hotel, I have a lot to say to you.

Zilang, the 21st.

Juhua:

This is the last word: please answer me earnestly.

You are too unforgiving of me, you must get married when it is impossible to get married, isn't this intentionally wounding people's happiness? I am extremely opposed to such a forced union.

Now I frankly say: we might as well dissolve the engagement, because marriage cannot be carried out under pain. What do you think? Please give me a responsible answer. Wishing you well, Zilang, the 28th.

Clerk Communication

The Oppression of the Environment 178

Editor Sir:

I am an apprentice in a shop, only sixteen years old this year, and have received higher primary school education. Because of difficult family circumstances, I was unable to continue my studies and obtain higher knowledge. This is something I deeply regret every time I think about it!

It was in the spring of last year, after I graduated from school, that I was oppressed by the above-mentioned environment, and with the recommendation of a friend of my father, I came to Shanghai, which is called the "Paris of the East" because of its prosperity, to learn a trade. During this past year, although I have been living a mechanical and meaningless life, sweeping the floor and wiping the counter every day, serving tea and cigarettes to customers, and sometimes running errands for senior staff, my personal life has been temporarily stable. And there is still spare time to read books and newspapers. The manager's treatment of me is not very harsh, which is much more comfortable compared to those in the same position as me in other shops and factories.

However, according to my usual quiet observation, the price of the hard work of the senior apprentices who have just completed their terms is only three yuan per month, or five yuan per month. Even the senior staff members earn at most twenty or thirty yuan. Seeing them supporting their families, I always feel extremely strained, not to mention those gentlemen who like to roam around. Moreover, how easy is it to rise from an apprentice with three to five yuan per month to a senior staff member with twenty to thirty yuan per month in this semi-modern shop? Therefore, looking ahead, I cannot help but feel a chill!

My father is almost fifty years old. Although the family is still supported by my father's efforts, in the near future, this heavy burden will undoubtedly be shifted from my father's shoulders to mine. How can I, who have no ability at all, bear the burden of supporting my parents and raising my younger siblings? Therefore, after deep consideration, I have to prepare to abandon my current career with a bleak future, and want to engage in a more promising career. But how dare I act rashly in the current situation where I don't know what is needed and don't know where to turn!

Recently, I saw various facilities for the 60th anniversary in your newspaper, with a "Clerk Communication" column dedicated to answering difficult questions for the business community in this city. To me, it is like finding a bright lamp in a dark room. I dare not be presumptuous, but with twelve thousand points of enthusiasm, I hope

Sir, please point out a bright road for this young man who is wandering at the crossroads.

Xu Jueren, December 1, in Shanghai

Editor's note: Mr. Xu's letter aroused our infinite sympathy. Originally, under the current situation of increasingly serious world economic panic, most people are suffering from economic oppression, so you don't have to be discouraged because of this. As for finding a satisfactory job, it is originally a very difficult thing. Moreover, "doing one job and complaining about it" has become a common phenomenon. Those who work with silk and satin envy bank clerks; those who work in the coal industry want to switch to the cloth industry. But wasn't there a common saying in the past that "every profession produces a champion"? This means that as long as you are willing to work hard, there will be a day to stand out. Therefore, we dare not easily agree with Mr. Xu's proposal. If there is a better and more promising career, it is of course better to change to it, but it also depends on your interest in it. If you rashly use the amount of remuneration as the standard for changing careers, then we believe that there will be unimaginable dangers in the future.

Besides, the manager treats you very well, and you have free time to read books and newspapers. Among the current apprentices, as you said, "you can be considered comfortable." Regarding the pursuit of knowledge, if you are determined, it is not a problem. Now, after reading your letter carefully, your writing is very fluent. At the age of sixteen, you have such attainments, which shows that you have put a lot of hard work into reading books and newspapers. We hope that Mr. Xu will continue to work hard, and the future is indeed limitless!

As for your family problems, that is a matter for the future (because your father is only fifty years old). You must know that times are changing rapidly. As long as you can work hard in your studies and be diligent in your duties, waiting for the opportunity to come, it seems that you don't need to worry too much.

Finally, we will cite some examples as stimulants for your efforts. For example, Mr. Shen Jiucheng, the founder of Sanyou Industrial Society, started out making handicrafts weaving pants and clothes straps: Mr. Bi Yuncheng, the director of the Yufeng Yarn Factory office, started out as a typesetter in the Commercial Press: Mr. Yang Sisheng, the founder of the late Pudong Middle School, started out as a mason; Mr. Ye Chengzhong, the school owner of Chengzhong Middle School, started out rowing a sampan: In addition, Mr. Mu Ouchu and Mr. Yu Qiaqing all struggled out of hardship. In the future, if we have time, we plan to introduce the history of the above-mentioned gentlemen to the readers as a model.

Simple Regulations for the Clerk Communication Column 179

㈠ Purpose of the Communication: This column aims to gather ideas, explain difficult problems, learn from each other, and increase the happiness of life.

㈡ Target of the Communication: The target of this column is limited to clerks and apprentices in terms of people, and limited to this port in terms of location.

㈢ Content of the Communication: Everything related to personal daily life, such as:

㈠ Occupation ㈡ Moral and academic cultivation ㈢ Entertainment and sports ㈣ Marriage and other issues, as well as other issues related to the country and society, are all welcome.

If the content of the problem is too profound and beyond the ability of this column, it can also be introduced to the newspaper's "Reader Advisor" for answering.

㈣ Method of Submission

㈠ The name, age, native place, occupation, and detailed mailing address must be written at the end of the letter: it must be continued to be written in subsequent letters.

㈡ The style of the letter is not limited, but it should be simple and easy to understand, and it must be written clearly.

㈢ Please write the words "Clerk Communication Column of the Local Supplement of Shenbao" on the face of the letter: If you need a reply, please attach two cents of postage.

㈣ The communicators must cut out the special stamp of this column and paste it on the upper left corner of the letter. No answer will be given if it is not pasted.

㈤ Handling Method After Receiving the Letter

㈠ All issues discussed that the newspaper believes have value in contributing to the public will be disclosed in the newspaper.

㈡ In order to respect the opinions of the communicators, all letters that state that they do not want to disclose their names, or that need to be answered separately, can also be handled accordingly.

㈢ If the communicators hope to disclose the letter in the newspaper, but the length is too long and the full text cannot be disclosed, it should be published selectively. Also, if the content of the problem is complicated and has to be studied carefully, resulting in a late answer or disclosure, readers are requested to understand. ㈣ When there is a congestion of letters, answers will be given in the order in which the letters are received, and readers are requested to understand if there are any delays.

Novel

The Sympathizer (Continuation 4) 181

— Zhang Henshui

㈢ All Misunderstand

Meng Guobao sat in the quiet environment, only cracking melon seeds and thinking about things. Before he knew it, he had finished the plate of melon seeds. It was probably quite late, and he had heard Sister-in-law Wang Er yawn twice. Knowing that the villagers went to bed early and he shouldn't disturb them from sleeping, lest they become unhappy, he stood up and said, "Old Er, thank you for the tea and melon seeds. I'll come to talk to you tomorrow morning. Will you be home?" Wang Laoer said, "Sure, sure, I'll come back a little earlier for the midday meal." Meng Guobao also said, "Sister-in-law Wang Er, thank you, see you tomorrow." Sister-in-law Wang Er was flustered and couldn't reply with anything else, just stood and smiled, so Meng Guobao went back happily. He had parents, elder brothers and sisters-in-law, and nephews and nieces at home, so it was a big family. His father and elder brothers gave him the money earned from the fields each year to pay for his tuition, hoping that he would become an official in the future and change the family's status. Of course, this money would all come back. Now, although he hadn't become an official, he was a university student. In the past two years, the old gentry in the countryside, those who were graduates of the imperial examinations, were all overthrown. In the past, the graduates of the imperial examinations would judge right and wrong for the villagers and act as witnesses, but now it was all changed to be handled by students who had returned from the provincial capital, Nanjing, Beijing, or Shanghai. In other words, students would act as the rural gentry. As such, Meng Guobao was also a quasi-gentry. Moreover, when Meng Guobao returned, many gentlemen from the Third District of the Shuanglukou Township Autonomous Association were interacting with him. This Third District was a small county government, and Meng Guobao was on good terms with those people, which showed that he was different from the ordinary. Therefore, Meng Guobao's father, Meng Erlaodie, and his elder brothers Guooqi and Guohua, were all very happy. While Guobao was enjoying the cool air on Wang Laoer's threshing ground, Erlaodie went outside the threshing ground to peek several times. None of the family members dared to sleep. When he came back, Erlaodie greeted him at the door and first asked with a smile, "You and Wang Laoer were talking so well, but he's a useless person." Meng Guobao sighed and said, "Alas! He is an oppressed person!" Erlaodie was a person who had read a few old books, so he understood the meaning of these words, and said, "No one is bullying him." Meng Guobao said, "Doesn't he not have his own land, and cultivates other people's land?" Erlaodie said, "That's right! He cultivates one dan of seeds for Mr. Wang Zibin, and one dan and two dou of seeds for Mr. Wang Youdao." Meng Guobao said in a loud voice, "He is a person controlled by big landlords, isn't he an oppressed person?" Erlaodie still didn't quite understand these words. But his son was a university student, and what he said had some reason, so he couldn't refute it anymore, and followed him into the door. Inside the door was a square courtyard, and all the family members were sitting there enjoying the cool air. When he came in, they all stood up. His mother greeted him with a smile and said, "Are you still writing tonight? I've already lit a mosquito coil in your room and put a pot of cool tea on the table." Meng Guobao said, "Oh! There's cool tea on the table? I put a book on economics on the table." His mother said, "A book, it doesn't matter if a little water spills on it, it'll dry in a while." Meng Guobao said, "How can it not matter? That book cost eight yuan." These seemingly unimportant words caused the family to gasp in unison.

Shenbao Architecture Weekly

Aim of Publishing Shenbao Architecture Special 182

— Editor

Today's world is a world of evolution. Today's academics are specialized academics.

Only when academics tend to specialization can there be evolution. And only when it tends to evolution can it not but excel in what it specializes in. Measuring the world with this, and exploring academics with this, whether it is politics, military affairs, education, or economy, the principle is the same.

Now, everything in the world, commentators say, cannot be outside of economics. To say that architecture is civil engineering, its art is a specialized science, and its effect is within the scope of economics. We in Shanghai, let's just talk about Shanghai. Shanghai is a world-famous commercial port, and especially an important commercial port in East Asia. Its economic relationship with China and even the whole world is self-evident. Therefore, its architectural undertakings are more numerous than in other places. In other words, judging by cause and effect, it may not be impossible to say that the multitude of Shanghai's architecture is what promotes Shanghai's development.

We have been running a daily newspaper for years. Since the daily newspaper evolves with the progress of the world, it should strive for specialization in line with the trend of world academics. The daily newspaper contains

nothing is too far, nothing is left out. In terms of the historical system, it is a general history, a historical material. But in terms of the academic standpoint, it may be incomplete or not specialized in its divisions. The effect is naturally less. This is the difference between the general history and the specialized systematic record. Without fully realizing its strengths or completing its purpose, we have been working tirelessly to improve ourselves to serve our readers.

Recently, in commemoration of the 60th anniversary of this newspaper, we have been working on innovation and at the same time devoting ourselves to specialized academics. We are committed to making this newspaper, in addition to general history and historical materials, also serve as a systematic record for the academic community. In order to seek sequentially and weigh the near and far, this newspaper is based in Shanghai, so we will first take Shanghai as

— Shen Tong

The owner of the Metheurst Apartments is Hengye Real Estate Co., Ltd., located at the intersection of Metheurst Road and Jing'an Temple Road. The style is very beautiful, designed by New Rehe Foreign Firm. It is the most modern apartment and is now under construction.

the dependence. The prosperity of Shanghai and the development of the architectural industry are the central pivots of industry and commerce, each with its own strengths. Therefore, this newspaper created an architectural special issue as a starting point.

The mission of this publication can be roughly stated as having two ends. One is to arouse public interest in architecture, thereby directly developing the architectural industry and indirectly consolidating the prosperity of Shanghai. The other is to provide faithful and systematic architectural historical materials, and to have experts write and provide strict guidance and criticism, so as to promote the progress of modern architectural undertakings, and to provide a basis for later architectural historians. With these two ends in mind, we will diligently seek and collect various patterns, records, statistics, and news, so as to make this publication a dynamic history in order to adapt to the environment and dedicate ourselves to specialization.
